Readers are cautioned not to place undue reliance on\nsuch forward-looking statements.', u'\n', u'1\n', u' PAGEBREAK ', u'\n', u'\n', u'\xa0', u'\n', u'\n', u'Forest City Enterprises, Inc. and Subsidiaries', u'\nSupplemental Operating Information', u'\n', u'Corporate Overview', u'\n', u'Corporate Description', u'\n', u'Founded in 1920 and publicly traded since 1960, Forest City Enterprises, Inc.\n(\x93FCE\x94 or the \x93Company\x94) is principally engaged in the ownership, development,\nmanagement and acquisition of commercial and residential real estate properties\nin 20 states and the District of Columbia. At July\xa031, 2004, we had\napproximately $7.2\xa0billion in total assets. We have a portfolio of real estate\nassets diversified both geographically and among property types. We operate our\nbusiness through four strategic business units as follows:\n\n\n\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\x95', u'\n', u'\xa0', u'\n', u'Commercial Group, our largest business unit, owns, develops, acquires and\noperates regional malls, specialty/urban retail centers, office buildings,\nhotels and mixed-use projects;', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\x95', u'\n', u'\xa0', u'\n', u'Residential Group owns, develops, acquires and operates residential\nrental properties, including upscale and middle-market apartments,\nadaptive re-use developments and supported-living facilities;', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\x95', u'\n', u'\xa0', u'\n', u'Land Development Group acquires and sells both land and developed lots to\nresidential, commercial and industrial customers. It also owns and\ndevelops land into master-planned communities and mixed-use projects; and', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\x95', u'\n', u'\xa0', u'\n', u'Lumber Trading Group, a lumber wholesaler.', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'Operating and Financial Information', u'\n', u'Financial Measures', u'\n', u'This supplemental package contains certain financial measures prepared in\naccordance with the generally accepted accounting principles (\x93GAAP\x94) under the\nfull consolidation accounting method, and certain financial measures prepared\nin accordance with the pro-rata consolidation method, (non-GAAP). Along with\nnet earnings, we use an additional measure, Earnings before Depreciation,\nAmortization and Deferred Taxes (\x93EBDT\x94), to report operating results. EBDT is\na non-GAAP financial measure and may not be directly comparable to\nsimilarly-titled measures reported by other companies. We believe the financial\nmeasures presented under the pro-rata consolidation method, comparable net\noperating income (\x93NOI\x94) and EBDT provide supplemental information about our\noperations. Although these financial measures are not presented in accordance\nwith GAAP, we believe they are necessary to understand our business and\noperating results, along with net earnings and other GAAP financial measures.\nOur investors can use these non-GAAP financial measures as supplementary\ninformation to evaluate operating performance. Our non-GAAP financial measures\nare not intended to be performance measures that should be regarded as\nalternatives to, or more meaningful than, our GAAP financial measures.\n\n\n\n', u'Pro-Rata Consolidation Method', u'\n', u'We present certain financial amounts under the pro-rata method, because we\nbelieve this information is useful to investors as this method more accurately\nreflects the manner in which we operate our business. This is because, in line\nwith industry practice, we have made a large number of investments in which our\neconomic ownership is less than 100% as a means of procuring opportunities\nand sharing risk. Under the pro-rata consolidation method, we present our\ninvestments proportionate to our share of ownership. Under GAAP, the full\nconsolidation method is used to report partnership assets and liabilities as\nconsolidated at 100% if deemed to be under our control or if we are deemed to\nbe the primary beneficiary for our investments in the variable interest\nentities (\x93VIE\x94), even if our ownership is not 100%. We provide reconciliations\nfrom the full consolidation method to the pro-rata consolidation method\nthroughout our supplemental package.\n\n\n', u'Certain amounts in the\nConsolidated Balance Sheets Information and Consolidated Earnings Information are not comparable to the prior period due to the implementation of\nFIN No.\xa046 (R) at February\xa01, 2004, and the consolidation of four properties previously accounted under\nthe equity method due to the acquisition of our partners\x92 interest.\n\n\n', u'EBDT ', u'- We believe that EBDT, along with net earnings, provides us, as well as\nour investors, additional information about our core operations and is\nnecessary to understand our operating results while property dispositions,\nacquisitions or other factors can affect net earnings in the short-term, we\nbelieve EBDT presents a more consistent view of the overall financial\nperformance of our business from period-to-period. EBDT is used by the chief\noperating decision maker and management to assess operating performance and\nresource allocations by business unit and on a consolidated basis. EBDT is\nsimilar to funds from operations (\x93FFO\x94), a measure of performance used by\npublicly traded Real Estate Investment Trusts (\x93REITS\x94), but may not be\ndirectly comparable to similarly titled measures reported by other companies.\n(See pages 29-32 for additional discussion of EBDT as well as a reconciliation\nof EBDT to net earnings.)\n\n\n\n', u'2\n', u'\n', u' PAGEBREAK ', u'\n', u'\n', u'\xa0', u'\n', u'\n', u'Forest City Enterprises, Inc. and Subsidiaries', u'\nSupplemental Operating Information', u'\n', u'Supplemental Operating Information', u'\n', u'The operating data contained in this document includes: occupancy data,\ncomparable NOI, reconciliation of NOI to net earnings, retail and office lease\nexpirations, significant retail and office tenant listings and our development\npipeline. The term \x93comparable,\x94 which is used throughout this document, is\ndefined as including properties that were opened and operated in both three and\nsix month periods ended July\xa031, 2004 and 2003.\n\n\n', u'We believe occupancy rates, retail and office lease expirations base rent, and\nsignificant retail and office tenant listings represent meaningful operating\nstatistics about our Company. This information will give interested parties a\nbetter understanding and more information about the operating performance of\nour Company.\n\n\n', u'Comparable NOI is useful because it measures the performance of the same\nproperties on a period-to-period basis and, along with EBDT (as discussed\nbeginning on page 29) is used to assess operating performance and resource\nallocation of our core business units. While property dispositions,\nacquisitions or other factors can impact net earnings in the short term, we\nbelieve comparable NOI gives a more consistent view of our overall financial\nperformance from quarter-to-quarter and year-to-year. A reconciliation of net\nearnings, the most comparable financial measure calculated in accordance with\nGAAP, to NOI and a reconciliation from NOI to comparable NOI are provided on\npages 6-9 of this document. A reconciliation of NOI to net earnings for each\nstrategic business unit can be found on pages 33-44.\n\n\n\n', u'Corporate Office', u'\nForest City Enterprises, Inc.', u'\nTerminal Tower', u'\n50 Public Square, Suite\xa01100', u'\nCleveland, Ohio 44113\n\n\n', u'SEC Form\xa010-K', u'\n', u'A copy of the Annual Report on Form 10-K as filed with the United States\nSecurities and Exchange Commission can be found on our website or may be\nobtained without charge upon written request to:', u'\n', u'Thomas T. This is because, in line with\nindustry practice, we have a large number of investments in which our economic\nownership is less than 100% as a means of procuring opportunities and sharing\nrisk. u'\xa0', u'\n', u'As is customary within the real estate industry, we invest in certain\nreal estate projects through joint ventures. We often provide funding of\nour partners\x92 equity contributions for the development and construction of\nreal estate projects. The most significant partnership for which we\nprovide funding is related to Forest City Ratner Companies, representing\nthe Commercial Group\x92s New York City operations. Our partner is the\nPresident and Chief Executive Officer of Forest City Ratner Companies and\nis the cousin to five executive officers of our Company. At July\xa031, 2004\nand January\xa031, 2004 amounts advanced in the normal course of business for\ndevelopment and construction of real estate projects on behalf of this\npartner, collateralized by this partnership interest, were $88,472 and\n$114,164 of the $330,997 and $313,160, respectively, presented above for\n\x93Advances to other real estate affiliates.\x94 These advances entitle us to a\npreferred return on and of the outstanding balances, which are payable\nfrom cash flows of each respective property. Effective February\xa01, 2004,\nwe modified certain provisions of our arrangement with our partner in the\nNew York operations for certain existing and all prospective property\npartnerships. These modifications had, and are expected to have, an\ninsignificant financial impact on us. During the first quarter of\n2004, the Company has reclassified in its Consolidated Balance Sheet a net amount\nof approximately $30,000 from investments and advances to real estate\naffiliates to minority interest, which has no impact to its\nConsolidated Statements of earnings or cash Flows.', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'We implemented FIN No.\xa046 (R) on February\xa01, 2004. As a result, we determined\nthat we are the primary beneficiary of 25 previously unconsolidated VIEs\nrepresenting 14 properties (19 VIEs representing eight properties in\nResidential Group, five VIEs/properties in Commercial Group and one\nVIE/property in Land Development Group). Of these 25 VIEs, 14 VIEs representing\n13 properties (nine VIEs/properties representing properties in Residential\nGroup, four VIEs/properties in Commercial Group and one VIE/property in Land\nDevelopment Group) that were previously accounted for using the equity method\nof accounting have been consolidated. The remaining 11 VIEs representing one\nproperty, (10 VIEs in Residential Group and one VIE/property in Commercial\nGroup) that were previously accounted for using the cost method of accounting\nhave also fully been consolidated. In addition, the Company deconsolidated five\nproperties that were previously consolidated.\n\n', u'28\n', u'\n', u' PAGEBREAK ', u'\n', u'\n', u'\xa0', u'\n', u'\n', u'Forest City Enterprises, Inc. and Subsidiaries', u'\nSupplemental Financial Information', u'\n', u'Results of Operations', u'\n', u'Net Earnings ', u'\x97 Our Net Earnings for the three months ended July\xa031, 2004 were\n$34,823,000 versus $6,603,000 for the three months ended July\xa031, 2003. Net\nearnings for the six months ended July\xa031, 2004 were $42,026,000 versus\n$21,395,000 for the six months ended July\xa031, 2003. The positive fluctuation\nfor this year compared to prior year is primarily attributable a gain on sale\nof $19,341,000 related two regional malls and one specialty retail center\nduring the second quarter of 2004. The positive fluctuation is also\nattributable to the addition of eight residential communities, four office\nbuildings and two retail centers. In addition, we experienced increased land\nsales in the Land Development Group and increased earnings in the Lumber\nTrading Group.\n\n\n', u'Net Operating Income from Real Estate Groups ', u'- NOI, a non-GAAP measure, is\ndefined as revenues (excluding straight-line rent adjustments) less operating\nexpenses (including depreciation and amortization for non-real estate\ngroups)\nplus equity in earnings of unconsolidated entities (excluding gain on\ndisposition of equity method operating properties) plus equity method\ndepreciation and amortization. We believe NOI provides us, as well as our\ninvestors, additional information about our core business operations and, along\nwith earnings, is necessary to understand our business and operating results.\nUnder the full consolidation method (GAAP), NOI from the combination of the\nCommercial Group and the Residential Group (\x93Real Estate Groups\x94) for the three\nmonths ended July\xa031, 2004 was $130,885,000 compared to $109,776,000 for the\nthree months ended July\xa031, 2003, a 19.2% increase. NOI for the Real Estate\nGroups was $245,375,000 for the six months ended July\xa031, 2004 compared to\n$212,567,000 for the six months ended July\xa031, 2003. This increase over the\ncomparable period in the prior year is primarily attributable to NOI generated\nfrom new properties which include nine residential communities, three office\nbuildings and one retail center opened during the year ended January\xa031, 2004,\nas well as the three residential communities, one office building and two\nretail centers opened thus far in 2004. A reconciliation of NOI to the most\ncomparable GAAP measure, net earnings, is presented on pages 8-9. A\nreconciliation of NOI to net earnings for each strategic business unit can be\nfound on pages 33-34.\n\n\n', u'Management also analyzes property NOI using the pro-rata consolidation method\nbecause it provides operating data at our ownership share, and we publicly\ndisclose and discuss our performance using this method of consolidation to\ncompliment our GAAP disclosures. Under the pro-rata consolidation method, NOI\nfrom the Real Estate Groups for the three months ended July\xa031, 2004 was\n$127,348,000 compared to $109,393,000 for the three months ended July\xa031, 2003,\na 16.4% increase. Under the pro-rata consolidation method, NOI for the Real\nEstate Groups was $236,932,000 for the six months ended July\xa031, 2004 compared\nto $214,064,000 for the six months ended July\xa031, 2003. Comparable NOI for the\nsecond quarter results improved substantially over the first quarter,\nresulting in a total Company comparable NOI increase of 1.8% for the\nfirst half of the year. Our\nretail portfolio continues to be the strongest segment of our\nbusiness, with comparable NOI for our retail portfolio up 2.7% year\nto date. See pages\xa05-7 for more detail.\n\n\n\n', u'EBDT ', u'- We use an additional measure, along with net earnings, to report our\noperating results. This non-GAAP measure, referred to as Earnings Before\nDepreciation, Amortization and Deferred Taxes (\x93EBDT\x94), is not a measure of\noperating results or cash flows from operations as defined by GAAP and may not\nbe directly comparable to similarly-titled measures reported by other\ncompanies.\n\n\n', u'We believe that EBDT provides additional information about our core operations\nand, along with net earnings, is necessary to understand our operating results.\nEBDT is used by the chief operating decision maker and management in assessing\noperating performance and to consider capital requirements and allocation of\nresources by segment and on a consolidated basis. We believe EBDT is important\nto investors because it provides another method for the investor to measure our\nlong term operating performance as net earnings can vary from year to year due\nto property dispositions, acquisitions and other factors that have a short-term\nimpact.\n\n\n', u'EBDT is defined as net earnings excluding the following items: i) gain (loss)\non disposition of operating properties, divisions and other investments (net of\ntax); ii) the adjustment to recognize rental revenues and rental expense using\nthe straight-line method; iii) non-cash charges from Forest City Rental\nProperties Corporation, a wholly-owned subsidiary of Forest City Enterprises,\nInc., for depreciation, amortization (including amortization of mortgage\nprocurement costs) and deferred income taxes; iv) provision for decline in real\nestate (net of tax); v) extraordinary items (net of tax); and vi) cumulative\neffect of change in accounting principle (net of tax).\n\n\n', u'EBDT is reconciled to net earnings, the most comparable financial measure\ncalculated in accordance with GAAP below. The\n\n\n\n', u'29\n', u'\n', u' PAGEBREAK ', u'\n', u'\n', u'\xa0', u'\n', u'\n', u'Reconciliation of Net Earnings to Earnings Before Depreciation, Amortization and Deferred Taxes (EBDT)', u'(2)', u'(continued)', u'\n', u'Forest City Enterprises, Inc. and Subsidiaries', u'\nSupplemental Financial Information', u'\n', u'adjustment to recognize rental\nrevenues and rental expenses on the straight-line method is excluded because it\nis management\x92s opinion that rental revenues and expenses should be recognized\nwhen due from the tenants or due to the landlord. We exclude depreciation and\namortization expense related to real estate operations from EBDT because we\nbelieve the values of our properties, in general, have appreciated over time in\nexcess of their original cost. Deferred taxes from real estate operations,\nwhich are the result of timing differences of certain net expense items\ndeducted in a future year for federal income tax purposes, are excluded until\nthe year in which they are reflected in our current tax provision. The\nprovision for decline in real estate is excluded from EBDT because it varies\nfrom year to year based on factors unrelated to our overall financial\nperformance and is related to the ultimate gain on dispositions of operating\nproperties. Our EBDT may not be directly comparable to similarly-titled\nmeasures reported by other companies.\n\n\n', u'Our EBDT for the three months ended July\xa031, 2004 grew by 41.3% to $70,995,000\nfrom $50,250,000 for the three months ended July\xa031, 2003. Our EBDT for the six\nmonths ended July\xa031, 2004 grew by 24.0% to $126,116,000 from $101,685,000 for\nthe six months ended July\xa031, 2003. The positive\nfluctuation is primarily also attributable to the addition of eight residential\ncommunities, four office buildings and two retail centers added to our portfolio in 2003 and 2004\nand a non-recurring\nexpense related to the write-off of bond issuance costs on bonds that were\nretired during the second quarter of 2003. In addition, we experienced\nincreased land sales in the Land Development Group and increased earnings in\nthe Lumber Trading Group.\n\n\n', u'Summary of EBDT ', u'- The information in the tables on pages 33-44 present amounts\nfor both full consolidation and pro-rata consolidation, providing a\nreconciliation of the difference between the two methods, as well as a\nreconciliation from NOI to EBDT to net earnings. Under the pro-rata\nconsolidation method, we present our partnership investments proportionate to\nour pro-rata share for each line item of our consolidated financial statements.\nUnder full consolidation, partnership assets and liabilities are reported as\nconsolidated at 100% if deemed under our control or if we are deemed to be the\nprimary beneficiary for investments in the VIEs, or an entity of SFAS No.\xa0144, assuming no significant continuing involvement, all earnings of properties and a division which have been sold or held for sale are reported as discontinued operations.\n\n\n', u'2) The\nCompany uses an additional measure, along with net earnings, to report its operating results.\nThis measure, referred to as Earnings Before Depreciation, Amortization and Deferred Taxes\n(\x93EBDT\x94), is not a measure of operating results as defined by generally accepted\naccounting principles and may not be directly comparable to similarly-titled measures\nreported by other companies. The Company believes that EBDT provides additional information\nabout its operations, and along with net earnings, is necessary to understand its operating results.\nEBDT is defined as net earnings excluding the following items: i) gain (loss)\xa0on disposition\nof operating properties, division and other investments (net of tax); ii) the adjustment to\nrecognize rental revenues and rental expense using the straight-line method; iii) noncash\ncharges from Forest City Rental Properties Corporation, a wholly-owned subsidiary of\nForest City Enterprises, Inc., for depreciation, amortization (including amortization of mortgage\nprocurement costs) and deferred income taxes; iv) provision for decline in real estate (net of tax);\nv) extraordinary items (net of tax); and vi) cumulative effect of change in accounting principle (net of tax).\n\n\n', u'3) Amount\nrepresents depreciation expense for certain properties accounted for on the equity method of accounting under both\nfull consolidation and pro-rata consolidation (a non-GAAP financial measure).  See our discussion of pro-rata consolidation in the preceding narrative.\nSee Investments and Advances to Real Estate Affiliates on pages 27-28 for discussion of these properties.\n\n\n', u'4) The Company recognizes minimum rents on a straight-line basis over the term of the related lease pursuant to the provision of SFAS No.\xa013, \x93Accounting for Leases.\x94 The straight-line rent adjustment is recorded as an increase or decrease to revenue from Forest City Rental Properties Corporation, a wholly-owned subsidiary of Forest City Enterprises, Inc., with the applicable offset to either accounts receivable or accounts payable, as appropriate.\n\n\n', u'5) The following table provides detail of Depreciation and Amortization.
